Most of the gamblers are prostitutes and low-class people. There are countless people who have fallen into this art. The gambling time is from noon to 12:00 midnight. Although the authorities have repeatedly negotiated to prohibit it, it has been fruitless due to the lack of sincere assistance from a certain party. Under this kind of situation, murders can happen at any time. At about 3:00 p.m. on the 3rd, Zhang Quan, a gambler by profession, who was 67 years old, also known as Xiaoquan and nicknamed Thirteen Flags, went to the Riguang Amusement Park to collect debts. He first had an argument with a clerk named Song Lao. Then Zhang injured his head with a teacup in an attempt to extort money. A Korean named Lin Shangqiao, who was working at the amusement park, thought that Zhang was intentionally disturbing the gambling den and stabbed Zhang in the head with a bayonet and threw him on the road on Qianmen Street. At this time, the gamblers in the amusement park were extremely dissatisfied with the situation and rushed out together and smashed the glass windows of the amusement park with bricks and stones. The storm escalated. Police officers from the Outer Fifth District heard the news and rushed to maintain order and reported to the Public Security Bureau, which informed the Japanese Police Department to send officer Sakata to the scene to jointly handle the negotiations. This incident alone shows the ferocity of the Koreans in Beiping. At about 5:00 p.m. on the 4th, another person, relying on the power of a certain party, rode a bicycle without buying a donation plate and went to the entrance of Dongjiaominxiang. He was discovered by the police and gendarmes on duty and an argument broke out. A soldier from a certain country came out to help him and took the gendarme away. The police officer asked why he was arresting the gendarme, but the police officer was also taken away. After the authorities negotiated with a certain party, he was released that night.

Rice Prices Soar in Southern Fujian 46

A Large Amount Has Been Shipped to Shantou Again in the Past Week

Xiamen Rice Industry Asks to Temporarily Withdraw the Tax on Foreign Rice

Xiamen Correspondence: Although the late rice harvest in Fujian Province this year was originally abundant, rice prices in Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Zhangzhou have risen day by day. The reason is that rice produced in eastern Fujian and Zhangzhou is transported out. The public outlet is Shantou, and the secret outlet is Taiwan. Rice in Zhangzhou rose by 20-30 cents in the middle of last month due to the transportation to Shantou. Later, the price in Shantou fell temporarily, and the price also returned to normal. At the end of the month, a rice merchant in Zhangzhou was entrusted to secretly purchase 8,000 piculs to be transported to Taiwan, and the price suddenly rose by 50 cents. At the beginning of this month, the price of rice in Shantou rose to 9 yuan again. Starting from the 1st of this month, rice stored in Xiamen has been continuously shipped to Shantou. White Zhan rice has risen from 6.7 yuan to 6.9 yuan, and coarse Zhan has risen from 6.2 yuan to 6.45 yuan. According to rice merchants, Shantou is implementing a full tax on foreign rice, and rice merchants are competing to purchase domestic rice. In addition to purchasing from Shanghai and Wuhu, they are also purchasing from Zhangzhou. At present, the price of rice in Shanghai and Wuhu is rising, and it is unprofitable to transport it to Shantou, so they are all turning to Zhangzhou. In recent days, rice merchants in Shantou have purchased more than 1,000 bags in Shima. At the same time, various counties along the coast of Zhangzhou, such as Pinghe, Zhao'an, Yunxiao, Zhangpu, and Nanjing, mostly use sailing ships to transport it directly for export. Longxi, Tianbao, Jiangdong Bridge, and Changtai transport it to Shima for transshipment for export. Each picul can make a profit of about one yuan. Although the price of grain and rice in Shima has risen, very few people from other villages come to the wharf to sell grain, so the rice mills have no grain to grind and the rice stocks are empty. On the other hand, the counties of Yongchun in Quanzhou have also increased the export of rice and grain and prohibited the export. At present, this chaotic phenomenon has caused unease among the people in southern Fujian. In Fuzhou, the price of rice has risen by 40 cents in the past week, reaching 9.6 yuan, with the momentum to break through the 10 yuan mark. However, most of the rice exported does not pass through customs and is smuggled, so there is no exact number to verify. Except for the publicly transported to Shantou, which has a verifiable quantity, the rest is unknown. In the midst of this rice panic, the Xiamen Rice Industry Association and the Hong Kong Industry Association responded to the Guangdong Provincial Government and submitted a petition to the Chamber of Commerce on the 5th requesting to telegraph the Executive Yuan to temporarily withdraw the foreign rice tax. The original text is as follows:

"We have found that the price of rice and grain in the market has recently soared due to the urgent need for rice in Guangdong Province and the absorption of rice from Shantou, resulting in a shortage of food in southern Fujian and high prices. If we do not seek relief urgently, the people's food will be worrisome. Fujian is not a rice-producing area. Even in times of good harvest, it still needs a large amount of foreign rice to supply. Since the customs levied a full tax on foreign rice, this foreign rice has disappeared. Food from all parts of the country is also very expensive, so there is no emergency relief. I am afraid that the grain will be expensive and hurt the people in the future. The foreign rice tax was originally to prevent dumping, and it should be adjusted according to the domestic food situation. Now that there is a food shortage, it seems appropriate to temporarily abolish it and restore it after the spring grain is abundant. Therefore, we hereby petition your association to telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to approve the temporary withdrawal of the foreign rice tax, and the people of Fujian will be deeply grateful." (December 6th)

Current Affairs Commentary

Legislative Principles of Inheritance Tax 47

— Li

The Central Political Committee recently passed ten inheritance tax principles and sent them to the Legislative Yuan for review. It is expected that the legislative process can be completed soon, and this new tax may be levied next spring. We have said before that inheritance tax is a good tax in the modern tax system, but in the process of this legislation, we cannot help but worry about whether this new tax, which is being created, can be implemented successfully in the future. We believe that the legislative authorities cannot simply seek convenience in the collection method, otherwise, there will definitely be many obstacles after implementation. We would like to put forward two points based on what we have seen.

First, inheritance tax has two types of systems: gross inheritance tax and separate inheritance tax. Both have their advantages and disadvantages. The advantage of the former is that the tax rate is simple, the investigation and collection procedures are simple, and the financial income is also higher. The disadvantage is that it does not ask about the number of heirs and the closeness of the relationship between the heir and the deceased and collects the same amount of tax for the same amount of gross inheritance, which is not very consistent with the principle of taxability and the principle of fair burden. The latter determines the tax rate based on the closeness of the relationship between the heir and the deceased and the number of heirs. It is very fair and consistent with the principle of taxability. The disadvantage is that the investigation and collection procedures are more complicated, and the financial income is also less. How should we choose between the two? Although the legislation of various countries is different, not many have adopted the former, and the general trend is to adopt a mixture of the two systems. Our country's inheritance tax should, of course, consider the beneficial aspects of the national treasury revenue, but it must also strive to comply with the principle of taxability and the principle of fairness. Therefore, it is necessary to adopt the strengths of both of the above-mentioned collection systems.

Second, although there is a theory in legal studies that newly enacted laws can be implemented in phases and regions within the national territory, it is very harmful to adopt this theory in the inheritance tax law. Because if the inheritance tax law is implemented in phases and regions, the nationals under the same government will have different tax obligations to the state at the same time. This not only violates the principle of fair tax burden, but also makes it inevitable that the inheritors of the inheritance within the inheritance tax collection area will move to the area where inheritance tax has not yet been collected in order to evade tax obligations. This will also add a layer of difficulty to the execution of the household registration law and the conscription law. The provisional regulations on inheritance tax drafted by the Ministry of Finance this spring have the provision that "the date and area of implementation of these regulations shall be determined by order." If this contains the meaning of phased implementation, it should be revised.

We hope that the legislative authorities will pay attention to the above two points when creating the inheritance tax law. In addition, the government must also make several necessary efforts to promote the inheritance tax. For example, the household registration law should be strictly enforced, and the protection of the right to a name in the current Civil Code should be restricted so that people cannot use their inherent habits to use nicknames to break up their property to evade tax obligations. The government should also make considerable efforts internationally so that people do not take refuge in international forces to evade tax obligations. However, these are not matters within the scope of legislation.

The Pope's Condition Is Worrying: Shortness of Breath with Slight Fever; Heart Showing Signs of Weakness 48

(Rome) Pope Pius XI's condition is currently quite serious. It is reported that he is suffering from shortness of breath, with a slight fever, and there is concern that it may lead to influenza. The Pope's heart is quite weak, so his condition is considered worrying. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Vatican City. Furthermore, the Pope is greatly worried about the perilous situation of Catholics in Spain, which has further aggravated his condition. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch, 5th)

The Pope then received Cardinal Pacelli, the Secretary of State of the Vatican, in his bedroom for a meeting that lasted 45 minutes, and comforted his attendants, telling them not to panic. Although those around the Pope do not appear worried, they are deeply concerned about other complications due to the Pope's advanced age. The French National Assembly Expresses Confidence in the Blum Cabinet; Dissatisfaction with the Policy of Blocking Spain; Communist Assembly Members Abstain from Voting; Cracks Exposed in the People's Front 54

(Paris) Today was the second day of the National Assembly's debate on the government's foreign policy. As a result of the debate, Premier Blum proposed a vote of confidence on the government's foreign policy. The National Assembly voted on it, and it passed by a large majority of 350 votes to 171. Eighty-one Communist assembly members abstained from voting. It should be noted that today was the first time since the establishment of the People's Front government that a vote of confidence was proposed to the National Assembly, and it was also the first time that the Communist Party was unwilling to vote in favor of the People's Front government. The reason for this is the Blum Cabinet's decision to continue implementing the policy of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War. Before the National Assembly voted on the motion of confidence in the government, Premier Blum delivered a speech, which, although brief, was quite poignant. He first stated that France's foreign policy is based on two simple principles: France's own interests should transcend everything, and that France's peace and European peace cannot be separated. The Premier said, "All assembly members and the entire French people must agree to these two principles, because war and peace cannot be confined within the borders of one country. If we want to preserve our country from war, we must also try to prevent war from breaking out in other countries. This is something everyone should understand." The Premier continued, "Spain has only one legitimate government. If the Nationalist forces authorities were to achieve military victory, it would not only harm democracy, but also threaten peace. It is regrettable that several national governments do not understand this and cannot abide by the non-intervention agreement. However, it is not necessarily the case that the principle of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War can be abandoned for this reason. If we want to find a way to help the Spanish Republican government win, merely restoring trade relations with Spain may not be enough. It is necessary for the government to send troops and supply arms to assist the Spanish government in order to achieve practical results. But why has the Communist Party not proposed this method? It is because the party is also well aware of the danger of this method. In short, my beliefs remain the same as before, that the danger of a European war is imminent, and that it can only be saved by France's actions. So what are you criticizing the government for? Do you think the government is too afraid of war? Do you think the government has put too much effort into peace? If so, then the government is not afraid of this kind of criticism, because one day, if the situation requires it, I will say to the world with a firm attitude, 'We, France, are not afraid of war!' But when will the French government make this kind of statement? It will be when our country's territory is threatened, and it will be when the territory of a country whose maintenance we have signed to acknowledge is threatened." (At this point, the entire room applauded.) (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Paris) When the National Assembly voted on the motion of confidence in the government today, the Communist assembly members abstained from voting. Therefore, there seems to be a sign of division within the People's Front. In the evening, after the National Assembly adjourned, Premier Blum gave a speech to the press, stating that although Deputy Speaker of the National Assembly, Communist Assembly Member Duclos, gave a fierce speech, the cabinet has decided to continue to hold power and will not resign because of this. Blum added, "We have decided to continue to govern because we are aware of the seriousness of the current environment. If a cabinet upheaval were to occur, foreigners would not be able to understand France's attitude, and domestic public opinion would also be confused and at a loss. Our national strength would inevitably be weakened, and various social reforms would inevitably be halted. Therefore, the government will not do this. However, all future actions of the People's Front government must be supported by the parties participating in the People's Front with a spirit of fidelity and trust." Furthermore, the joint meeting of the representatives of the left-wing parties of the National Assembly will be held next Tuesday to discuss the issue of whether the Communist Party will continue to support the current government. At that time, if the Communist Party reiterates its cooperation with the Blum Cabinet, the political situation should be greatly clarified. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Japanese Financial Figure, Seinosuke Go, Retires 59

(Tokyo) Seinosuke Go, a prominent figure in the Japanese financial world, has been in poor health recently, and in view of the changing social situation, has long intended to retire from the financial world. Go suddenly announced his retirement to all parties concerned on the 5th, and resigned from all public positions except for his membership in the House of Peers. (Domei dispatch, 6th)

Churchill Publishes an Article Warning the British Cabinet to Proceed with Caution; To Follow the Procedures of Consulting with Parliament; Not to Coerce the King to Abdicate 60

(London) Prominent Conservative Member of Parliament Winston Churchill published an article today urging the public to remain calm, stating that the nation should understand the nature of the constitutional dispute. There is currently no conflict between the King and Parliament, and this matter has not yet been discussed with Parliament. The current issue is whether the King will abdicate on the advice of the cabinet members. It has never happened before that such advice has been given to the King. What we are encountering is the King's desire to do something that cannot succeed in any way, and has been doing so for five months. This act may never succeed for various reasons. Demanding the supreme sacrifice of abdication and potential exile has no constitutional basis. The cabinet has no authority to advise the King to abdicate. Only the most serious parliamentary procedures can raise this point in a firm manner. The cabinet has no right to act on its own without first exploring the wishes of Parliament. Churchill meant that this could be done by the King issuing an edict to Parliament, or by both Houses of Parliament submitting a memorial to the King. Conservative Member of Parliament Cripps also published an article today, agreeing with the government's attitude expressed by the Prime Minister, but stated that the advice to the King should be based on the national political interests, and not on the opinions of one individual or sect. He also said, "I believe that there is no sufficient reason to force the King to abdicate now, and I believe that the nation will never want to go to this extreme." (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Churchill also said that if the cabinet had obtained a guarantee from the leaders of the opposition parties in advance, that even if the cabinet resigned, the opposition parties would never come out and form a cabinet, it would be tantamount to presenting the King with an ultimatum. We should take a patient attitude now and not act rashly, because the act of demanding the King's abdication is extremely serious. Not only should Parliament constitutionally reaffirm its position in advance, but all methods that can achieve a more satisfactory solution should also be tried. In addition, there is still a question: What has been done so far? It is heard that the King has proposed that the cabinet submit a bill to Parliament (referring to the King's spouse not being able to set an example for the nation, and her children not being able to inherit the throne). As far as this matter is concerned, the cabinet can refuse to submit such a bill if it does not intend to, so why is it necessary to demand the King's abdication? (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(London) Regarding the marriage issue, after an address made by Churchill, a well-known Conservative Party Member of Parliament, the general public is wondering if the Cabinet members are to remain tranquil and prudent as a result of this address. Political insiders note that the address by Churchill would, without a doubt, leave an impression with the populace, though it is difficult to determine how it would affect the other Members of Parliament. What is clear is that the right-wing Conservative Party under the leadership of Churchill has always opposed Prime Minister Baldwin, and is likely to respond accordingly. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

International Attention 61

(London) International attention remains focused on the dispute between the British King and the Cabinet over the marriage issue, with the United States paying particular attention. Only the German newspapers have not published a single word on the matter. Washington officials believe that the British King is one of the few balancing forces in this turbulent world, and that any change would have repercussions. Therefore, they hope that Britain can overcome all crises without harming the King's authority. This hope reflects the general sentiment in the United States. The French press's tone on the matter is mostly sympathetic to both the King and Britain. The Paris newspapers all believe that the King's abdication is the only solution. Italy is paying close attention to the matter and expresses great sympathy for the difficulties experienced by the King, Parliament, and the British Empire. The Soviet newspapers only publish the events and news about Mrs. Simpson, without any commentary. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

The British King's Will is Firm; Struggling for Both His Throne and His Beloved; May Resort to Abdication; Busy Meetings at Downing Street 62

(London) Concerning the issues surrounding the King and his desire to marry Wallis Simpson, there has been a great upsurge in support for the King by the populace and the press in recent days. Labour MP Jack Khut began to spread word of a pro-King movement nationwide. Thousands of people have also been marching in the streets of London, shouting slogans demanding the King's freedom to choose his spouse, and calling Mrs. Simpson "our new queen." General Secretary of the Liverpool Postal Worker's Union Hodgson summoned all the postal workers nationwide, and is to hold an assembly tomorrow. It is said that the following statement would be issued, "all postal workers support the King, but merely hope that the King protect the Constitution."

It is said that the King not only would not concede on Mrs. Simpson, but did not plan to abdicate either. He is to fight for both his lover and the throne. It is further understood that former Chancellor of the Exchequer Churchill would replace Baldwin, as Churchill has allegedly told Baldwin, "feel free to proceed." The Cabinet is said to have three options: (1) to continue to strongly urge the King to give up Mrs. Simpson, (2) to soften their attitude, which is an unlikely path, or (3) to resign as a first step towards forcing the King to abdicate. It is said that the King would be able to sway national opinion as a show of support. If he were to garner the endorsement of Lord Rothermere's papers, which sell 60 million copies a day, he would topple the government as he had repeatedly done so in the past.

At the same time, Churchill issued a declaration today attacking the government and asking for more time to handle this unexpected problem. Churchill specifically warned the Cabinet not to force the King to abdicate. This declaration is set to be published in the Sunday papers, so it would have a great impact.

In short, the end of this week is an unfortunate time in British history, because no matter how the situation develops, the feelings of all parties have been greatly damaged, and it will take many years to recover. The King hopes that the public's opinion will show that they still want him to remain in the position. As for his marriage, it may not be approved by the general public. If the King were to abdicate, the Prime Minister would probably formally announce it in the House of Commons on Monday morning. The House of Commons would then postpone the meeting until Tuesday to resolve the succession of the Duke of York. The legislatures of the various dominions would also hold similar procedures on Wednesday. The Australian Parliament has scheduled a meeting for Tuesday, so observers feel that the situation is serious. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch, 5th)

(London) Regarding the marriage issue, there was hope for a turnaround in the situation after Conservative hardliner Churchill made an appeal the other day. Now, since the King has rejected this, it may end in failure. Although the various newspapers belonging to press baron Lord Rothermere have been attacking the government in recent days, when the lord's son went to visit the King at the Belvedere Fort yesterday, the King refused to see him. Therefore, political insiders believe that the King may announce his abdication this afternoon or tomorrow. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(London) King Edward has canceled any public meetings scheduled at this time to facilitate handling the current crisis. The most important events of the week are the inspection of the Scottish Guards at the Tower of London on Tuesday morning and the visit to the Staffordshire pottery factories on Wednesday and Thursday. Prime Minister Baldwin revisited the Belvedere Fort, where the King resides. Word has it that the Cabinet will be convening at 5-5:30 this afternoon. The Prime Minister arrived at Belvedere Fort at 6:30 last evening and met with the King for about an hour. Apparently, several documents were presented to the King. When the Prime Minister returned to 10 Downing Street at 8:30, his private secretary informed the press that "nothing more will happen tonight, no one will come here." But shortly after, Home Secretary Simon visited and met with the Prime Minister for two hours. At around 8 o'clock last night, a Royal Mail car drove from Belvedere Fort to London. Because the curtains were drawn, it was not known who was in the car. Other visitors to the Prime Minister at 10 Downing Street yesterday included the Prime Minister of Northern Ireland, Viscount Craigavon. Also, Inspector General Sir Somerville visited the Colonial Office yesterday. At the same time, the Archbishop of Westminster ordered priests and people to unite in prayer for the happiness of the King and the country. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(London) This morning, the Attorney General of Cornwall, Monckton, returned from Belvedere Fort in the suburbs, where the King resides, and immediately went to Downing Street to visit Prime Minister Baldwin and discussed the marriage issue. (The King was originally the Duke of Cornwall before being ennobled as Prince of Wales.) Lord Privy Seal MacDonald was also present. Afterwards, a large number of Cabinet members, including the MacDonalds, Home Secretary Simon, First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, Minister for Coordination of Defence Inskip, and President of the Board of Trade Runciman, convened at the Prime Minister's Office and the Prime Minister chaired the meeting. Responsible figures stated that the Cabinet members were preparing for the Cabinet meeting scheduled for 5:30 this afternoon. The Prime Minister then took a secretary and drove to Marlborough House to visit Queen Mary and returned to the Prime Minister's Office at 11:50 AM to continue the discussions with his Cabinet members. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(London) Regarding the dispute caused by the marriage issue, political insiders have claimed that the responsibilities of the Attorney General of Cornwall, Monckton, are extremely important. He is in frequent contact with the King, and before meeting with the Prime Minister this morning, he was with the King last night for a long time. If the King were to abdicate, his source of income would depend solely on Cornwall. (The King was the Duke of Cornwall before being ennobled as the Prince of Wales.) However, according to the constitution, the Duke of Cornwall is the King's eldest son, so if the newly established King already has an heir and Edward VIII still wants to receive income from Cornwall, then a new law must be passed. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

The Labor Party States: No Intention to Form a Cabinet 63

Unwilling to use the King's Private Life

as the Main Goal of the Election

(London) Regarding the marriage issue, Churchill, the leader of the extreme Conservatives, made a statement to the press yesterday, roughly saying that Major Attlee, the leader of the opposition Labour Party, had given Prime Minister Baldwin a guarantee that he would not come forward to form a cabinet. In addition to Attlee's personal denial, union officials have also commented on this matter, saying that the issue of forming a cabinet is not something that Major Attlee can decide on his own; it must be decided by the Labour members of the lower house. If these members wish to make a decision, they must convene the Labour Party National Executive Committee for discussion. (Note: The Labour Party National Executive Committee is composed of Labour Party members of parliament, the Labour Party, and the Trade Union Congress.) Labour Party officials say that regardless of the constitutional and religious disputes that the marriage issue may cause, their party has no intention of forming a new cabinet to prepare for a general election. Moreover, the British monarch originally occupies a position of arbitration between the various political parties. If an election is held because of the King's own problem, it will endanger the traditional status of the British monarch. This is also a concern for religious believers. In short, Labour Party officials urgently hope that the government authorities will inform the public of the situation before a cabinet crisis occurs and that things are not handled hastily. The Rothermere Newspaper Group Opposes the King's Abdication: 66

A Government that Disregards Public Opinion Will Find it Difficult to Exist

(London) The Evening News recently published a declaration by Lord Rothermere, the newspaper tycoon (who recently traveled around the world and passed through Shanghai), with the headline "Rothermere's Warning," which stated roughly: "You cannot drive away the greatest figure in contemporary Britain during the weekend holiday. (The meaning is the King's abdication.) I have just traveled around the world and can say with certainty that the people of all countries unanimously praise the current King. As for the marriage issue, it should be resolved over time. If it is done hastily, rumors will inevitably arise and affect the King's reputation. In short, any government that disregards public opinion on this matter will find it difficult to exist." (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Mrs. Simpson's Whereabouts After Arriving in France: Temporarily Residing in the Rogers Villa, Guarded by Police: Newspaper Reporters Unable to Enter 67

Nice: Mrs. Simpson is currently residing in the villa of Mr. and Mrs. Rogers. There are police guards in front of the door, and no one is allowed to enter. In the past two days, newspaper reporters and photographers from Paris and London have surrounded the villa, but they have not been able to enter. It is believed that Mrs. Simpson and her friends will not make any public statements. The rumor that she met with reporters on the way from Calais to the villa is not true. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(London) On her way to the Riviera, Mrs. Simpson passed through Vienne in western France. The first person she agreed to meet was a reporter from the Paris Evening News. It is said that she said, "I hope everyone understands that I need to rest quietly in my current environment. I am extremely tired now. The French are very kind, but very disturbing. Since yesterday, I have been followed everywhere I go." Mrs. Simpson continued to answer questions, saying, "I have no plans. Everything depends on the King of England's decision. I am retreating to rest quietly and await the King's decision." Mrs. Simpson tried her best to avoid public attention during her passage through France. When she was in Valence, she passed through many kitchen doors that had been closed for many years, and they were temporarily cleaned by servants. In Vienne, she passed through a cellar door to enter a restaurant. Last night, she arrived in Avignon, fifty miles from Marseille. At that time, her driver asked passers-by for directions to Aix-en-Provence. Later, at 11:35 p.m., she arrived at the village of Le Cannet, and stayed at the home of her American friends, Mr. and Mrs. Rogers. (Reuters News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Le Cannet: Mrs. Simpson arrived here by car at 11:30 tonight after leaving England and arriving in France. Previously, the King of England had called an American friend, Rogers. It is said that the King had indicated that he might abdicate and go to Le Cannet to meet Mrs. Simpson. The King of England's call to Rogers was to inform Rogers that Mrs. Simpson would arrive here soon and stay temporarily at Rogers' place. Tonight, the yacht of Mrs. Phipps, the widow of Prince Brollo of Monte Carlo, suddenly raised its sails and waited to depart. It is said that Mrs. Simpson may take it to avoid the noise in the Mediterranean. Today, a British detective came here by plane to protect Mrs. Simpson. The French government has also specially dispatched two detectives to guard Rogers' villa. At the same time, Rogers has strictly closed the doors and does not allow servants to go out. Before Mrs. Simpson came here, in order to avoid meeting newspaper reporters, she got up at 3:30 in the morning. After arriving in France, she detoured and had lunch at Vienne Station. Her attendant was Sir Brownlow, the former equerry. On the way to Valence, Mrs. Simpson stopped temporarily to talk to a passerby, who later said that Mrs. Simpson said, "Everything is decided by the King. I have no say. Although newspaper reporters are kind and amiable, they are too intrusive." (National Telegram, 5th)

US Army Seeks Modernization: Improve Coastal Defenses: Safeguard National Security 73

(Washington) It was learned here today that Major General Craig, Chief of Staff of the US Army, has submitted his annual report to the Secretary of the Army, stating that the US Army's modernization plan must be completed as soon as possible and not allowed to decline, so as to resist foreign aggression and guarantee national security. Craig praised the morale of the regular army but said that only a small part of the US military can fight immediately, while the military of other countries is already prepared and can fight both domestically and abroad. Therefore, the improvement of the US military is imperative for self-defense, and the US Army is very different from other countries. It not only has no power to invade others but also lacks a complete organization. The so-called regular army has very few people, and the strength to cope with war is far less, but its responsibility is very heavy. At present, only the field artillery brigade has been motorized, and there is also an anti-aircraft artillery brigade with modern equipment. As for chemical warfare supplies, although 20,000 gas masks have been prepared this year, many are still lacking, and 100,000 more should be added each year to meet the needs. Chahar-Beibei Bandit Puppet Army Suffers Heavy Losses in Counterattack on Bailing: A Certain Party Rectifies Bandit Troops and Plans to Counterattack Again: Bandit Morale Dispersed and Many Revolt and Surrender 74

Suiyuan Correspondence: Since our side recovered Bailing Temple, the only base in northern Sui that the puppet bandits had been preparing for a very long time was seized by the National Army. All of a certain party's plans to invade Sui over the years were taken by our forces. A certain party's ambition has not diminished. After the puppet bandit troops fled in disarray, on one hand, they concentrated on rectification in the Damaozi area, more than 100 li northeast of Bailing Temple, and on the other hand, they concentrated puppet bandits in Shangdu, Chahar, and transferred puppet troops from Rehe, attempting to invade again on both sides of eastern and northern Sui. In recent days, in addition to bandit planes visiting for reconnaissance every day, there has been no formal disturbance. The bandit planes also dare not fly low because they fear the accuracy of our anti-aircraft guns. Sure enough, at dawn on the 4th, the puppet bandits, consisting of the Wang Ying, Jin Jiashan, and Li Shouxin units, totaling 4,000 to 5,000 men, gathered at Damaozi and suddenly launched a counterattack on our side's position at Bailing Temple. There were also hundreds of ronin recruited by a certain party in Dalian, carrying cannons and light and heavy machine guns, and they launched a fierce attack on us. At the same time, eight or nine airplanes provided cover and carried out bombing. Our garrison all had the determination to advance without retreating and to be invincible, and the morale of our army's various units was extremely high. All felt honored to be able to go to the front to kill the enemy and regretted not being able to reach the front. Therefore, although the bandit puppets came fiercely, our army bravely stepped forward and met the attack. After 10 o'clock, the battle was very fierce. Our army became more and more courageous and fought with a hundred times the morale. The puppet bandits were ultimately a rabble, and the lure of money could not ultimately change their lives, so they fled again like rats. Our side also captured more than 200 bandits. According to the captured bandits, a certain party spends all day rectifying the puppet bandit troops and said that our army at Bailing Temple is very weak and can be taken immediately. A certain party actively supplements the puppet bandits with a large number of guns and distributes many airplanes and poison gas, etc. Although the puppet bandits suffered this heavy blow, they occupy the nearby two hilltops, attempting to counterattack again. Our garrison is not only determined to defend Bailing Temple but also has the ambition to eliminate the remaining bandits in Sui, and it is thought that there will inevitably be fierce battles in the next two or three days. The puppet bandits have suffered repeated heavy blows, and bandit morale is dispersed. The date of resolution should not be far off.

Chahar-Beibei Militias Revolt One After Another

According to talks with people from Xinghe, since the puppet bandits began to invade Xinghe on November 17, they have been repeatedly attacked fiercely by our garrison, merchants' associations, and security teams. The bandits completely collapsed on the 29th, and there is no trace of bandits in Xinghe. Only 700 to 800 puppet bandits Zhang Paodan (i.e., Zhang Wanqing) still occupy Nanchaoqian. (However, the bandits have no fighting spirit and are dispersing. Puppet bandit regiment commander Su Wanlong was indeed killed by our army. Wang Ying has not been seen since he fled alone from Honggeertu.) The people and militias of Chahar-Beibei, unable to withstand the oppression of the puppet bandits and stimulated by the nationwide patriotic movement, have revolted one after another. Several hundred have already surrendered to the Xinghe Security Office. It is rumored that a certain regimental commander of Li Shouxin's unit is preparing to declare independence. The Yihe Commercial Firm has opened its doors and is operating as usual, and people's hearts are also very stable.

Major Disaster in Honggeertu

In the battle of Honggeertu, the local people suffered huge losses. The Taolin County government sent people to conduct detailed surveys. Three or four tenths of the houses were destroyed, and three or four blockhouses were destroyed. A total of 22 people were killed and injured, including three women, with 11 deaths and 11 injuries. The county sent personnel to comfort them with money, with 10 yuan for each severely injured person and 6 yuan for each lightly injured person, ordering them to seek treatment nearby. After the puppet bandits invaded Yihe this time, the villagers in the county were looted and burned by the bandits, and the disaster situation was also serious. Now, the telegraph from Xinghe County Magistrate Meng Zhongwen requesting disaster relief from the Sui Provincial Government is recorded on the left to give a glimpse. Urgent: Chairman Fu, Civil Affairs Department Director Yuan, Finance Department Director Li Junjian, check that more than 20 villages, including Yaozigou, Dajiankou, Halagou, Village 29, Huangyuwa, Shuangnaobao, Village 3, Fuzhixiang, Village 16, Dahalacun, Xiahalacun in Xinghe District 1, and Qingyuxiang, Zhang Bayin Village, Haojiagangfang, Village 2, and Si Ni's Dengjia Village, Village 2, and Yushuwa in District 2, were all occupied by the puppet bandits this time. People, horses, grain, clothing, livestock were all looted, and several people were killed and injured. Houses were also burned. Now the bandits have retreated completely, but the disaster-stricken people in each village are displaced and without food or clothing at this time of cold weather. They are suffering from hunger and cold and are in a miserable state. We are supervising Deputy Security Director Han Jingyu and each instructor to conduct detailed surveys, provide appropriate comfort, and set up temporary shelters in nearby villages that have not been bandit-stricken to resettle the refugees and prevent them from freezing and starving. In addition to reporting the details of the disaster in a separate case, we respectfully report and request the allocation of disaster relief funds to help with relief. (4th)

North China Japanese Army and Navy Will Conduct Large-Scale Exercises in the Suburbs of Tianjin: Exercises Will Last Four Days, from the 9th to the 12th: Taking Tianjin City as the Target of Contention for Both Sides: 14th Fleet Will Be Long-Term Moored in Tanggu 75

Tianjin Correspondence: The "Aoi" and "Ogi" destroyers of the 14th Destroyer Division of the Japanese Lushun Naval Base arrived at Tanggu from Qinhuangdao and Lushun respectively on the morning of the 5th and moored in front of the Japanese barracks wharf. The destroyer team has a total of three warships. The "Kiku" warship arrived at Tanggu at the end of November. As of the 5th, Tanggu has berthed a team of Japanese destroyers. The North China Japanese Garrison Headquarters stipulates that from the 9th to the 12th of this month, from 9:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. every day, it will conduct land-sea coordination combat exercises in the area of Dabizhuang, Sunzhuang, and Fanzhuang in the suburbs of Tianjin in conjunction with the Marine Corps of the three warships of the 14th Destroyer Division, taking Tianjin City as the target of contention. The mobilization will be between 2,000 and 3,000 people, and the commander of the 14th Destroyer Division, Sometoshi Hisameteru, and the commander of the 2nd Infantry Regiment of the North China Garrison, Huangdao, will be responsible for the command. This is an unprecedented example in recent years. Commander Tadashi specially took a special train on the Beining Railway to Tanggu at 8:30 a.m. on the 5th with Infantry Brigade Commander Kawabe, Chief of Staff Hashimoto, Aide-de-Camp Sasaki, and Department Attachment Suzuki to inspect the Marine Corps of the three warships and to discuss the very cautious measures in the serious situation in North China with Commander Hisameteru, the commanders of the "Kiku," "Aoi," and "Ogi," Lieutenants Kaneko, Koga, and Kunibu, in the Tanggu barracks, before returning to Tianjin at 2:00 p.m. Kayashima will arrange the various matters of the exercise starting on the 6th. The chemical machine warfare team in the Dongjuzi barracks in Tianjin will also send a part of it to participate at that time.

The Qingdao Incident occurred, and the situation in Suiyuan became like a raging fire. After Tadashi and Hashimoto finished their military inspection in the Qinhuangdao-Yuyu-Tang area and returned to Tianjin on the 3rd, they convened an important meeting at the Haiguang Temple Headquarters at 2:00 p.m. on the 4th. Military Attaches Matsumuro and Hamada stationed in Pingjin, Brigade Commander Kawabe, Military Attache Obamoto stationed in Zhangjiakou, and Military Attache Hayama stationed in Suiyuan arrived early in the morning to participate. The Kwantung Army Department sent Lieutenant Colonel Fukushima Maruhei on the morning of the 3rd to wait in Tianjin with Okamoto, the staff officer of the Rehe garrison, to attend the meeting that day. The meeting discussed the current situation, diplomacy, military deployment, and the Suiyuan and Qingdao incidents in detail for a long time before adjourning at 5:00 p.m. Obamoto and Hayama flew back to Zhang and Sui on the morning of the 5th. Matsumuro had to rush to hand over because he was transferred to the commander of the 4th Cavalry Brigade and returned to Pingjin on the evening of the 5th. Before his successor Major General Matsui took office, he was temporarily maintained by Major Hamada. At the meeting on the 4th, the North China Garrison Headquarters considered that the attitude of the Navy side regarding the Qingdao Incident was not fully understood. In order to establish close contact, it sent Staff Officer Lieutenant Colonel Wakachi to Qingdao by Huizhou Company plane at 8:00 a.m. on the 5th to meet Commander Okawa of the 3rd Fleet to exchange opinions and to give instructions to Military Attache Taniogi stationed there. He will return to Tianjin on the 6th to report. According to observations of the Tianjin military headquarters' movements, if the Qingdao Incident expands, it may take unanimous action to support it remotely. As for the Navy, Commander Sometoshi Hisameteru of the 14th Destroyer Division, Commanders Kaneko and Koga of the "Kiku" and "Aoi," and Staff Officer Lieutenant Suzuki came to Tianjin from Qinhuangdao and Tanggu on the morning of the 4th. Chief of Staff Hara Chuuichi of the Lushun Naval Base and Staff Officer Kamite came to Tianjin on the night of the 3rd to convene an important meeting with the Tianjin Naval Attache Kubota and Lieutenant Colonel Kuwahara at the Tianjin Naval Attache Office on Qiushan Street at 10:00 a.m. on the 4th. Kubota presided over the meeting and discussed the current situation, the Qingdao Incident, and the so-called emergency situation, the Bohai Bay alert, and the coordination between the army and the navy to protect overseas Chinese in detail, and a concrete decision was made before adjourning at about 1:00 p.m. Chief of Staff Hara took a plane back to Lushun on the morning of the 5th to report the decision of this meeting to Commander Wada. The Japanese 14th Destroyer Division believes that North China is within its alert line and will be stationed in Tanggu for a long time. It originally planned to sail to Tianjin next week, but now the Haihe River is shallow, so it has to dock there temporarily. (5th)

After China's Opening to Navigation, Plans Emerge for Military Air Routes; Problems with the Longyan Mine and Jinshi Railway are Temporarily Suspended; Our Side Has Not Yet Recognized the Military Air Route Issue 76

Beiping Correspondence: Regarding the issue of economic cooperation between Hebei, Chahar, and Japan, since its commencement, the restoration of the Longyan Iron Mine and the construction of the Jinshi Railway have been decided upon successively. However, the Hebei-Chahar authorities have repeatedly stated that everything can be handled on the principle of not hindering national sovereignty and benefiting the people, and that it is preferable to invest. At the same time, Lu Zongyu was appointed to prepare for the Longyan Iron Mine, and the Communications Committee was responsible for building the Jinshi Road. Since the commencement, the part of the Longyan Iron Mine to be taken over is roughly in order, and there are also ways to raise funds for the debt. However, when it will be mined depends on when the funds are available. However, the authorities believe that the restoration and mining of Longyan should be invested by foreign parties and handled by our own side, which is in line with the principles they adhere to. Otherwise, it would be detrimental to national rights. The Japanese side hopes that it will be jointly run by China and Japan, so as to control half of the power. Since the opinions of both parties are different, this is the reason why it has been delayed. This issue is currently being studied by Lu Zongyu, who is in charge. Lu is negotiating everything in Tianjin, but it is said that there is no progress. The construction of the Jinshi Road is also temporarily suspended due to the different opinions of both parties on investment and joint operation. The relevant authorities are carefully considering the solution, and there are still some difficulties in realizing the facts. As for the navigation issue, it is being handled in accordance with the original plan of the former Political Affairs Readjustment Committee. Because the unauthorized flight of Japanese aircraft damages national rights, it is hoped that Japanese aircraft will stop flying immediately after the opening of navigation. This is why the Huitong Company was organized. After the company was established, the Japanese side once again expressed its intention to open military air routes. The authorities did not agree. The Japanese side then hoped to stipulate the military air period. This issue has not yet been resolved. According to a certain authority, the reason why the Japanese side raised this opinion is that the navigation between China and the the US, China and the UK, and China and Germany contains military characteristics. This is actually a misunderstanding, because these three lines are purely commercial and have no side effects. After explanation, it should not become a problem. The aviation training class is being handled by Liu Zhongtan, director of the education group of the company. Fifty students will be recruited and graduate in one year. The regulations have begun to be reviewed. Zhang Yunrong, chairman of the company, is quite negative. He is currently sick in Peiping and is being treated by a doctor. (4th)

Red Cross Relief Team Has Arrived at the Front; The General Tianjin United Team is Stationed in Jining; The Suiyuan Team Sets Off for Bailing Temple; The Chahar Team Sets Off for Datong 77

Ping News: The World Red Cross Society's 13th Joint Relief Team set off for Datong a few days ago. Japanese Transporting Smuggled Goods to Shandong; Han Fuqu Orders Detention and Transfer to Relief; Dozens of Japanese Go to the Provincial Government and Strongly Demand to See Han; Goods Detained are Returned by Koreans to the Japanese Consulate 78

Jinan Correspondence: The trend of smuggling has become very prevalent again recently. Although our customs anti-smuggling department has strictly investigated, it has not been curbed. Moreover, a certain party used the Jinpu Railway for transportation. After being blocked by the anti-smuggling department and unable to travel smoothly, it changed to using cars to travel south from Tianjin to sell in northern Shandong. Each time, Japanese and Koreans escorted the goods. Last month, officials from the Jinan anti-smuggling department discovered two smuggling cars in Luokou. Both the people and the goods were transported to Jinan. In a short time, hundreds of Japanese and Koreans arrived, demanding the return of the smuggled goods and beating and insulting the officials of the anti-smuggling department and the road police, rampaging and disregarding everything. Since then, their arrogance has become more intense, and they openly transport goods almost every day. Han Fuqu, chairman of Shandong Province, recently received an order to provide effective assistance to anti-smuggling work. Moreover, white powder drugs were openly carried in the smuggled goods, destroying the anti-drug results in Shandong Province. He then issued an order to all counties in northern Shandong to strictly investigate and arrest. After receiving the order, Wang Ying, the magistrate of Leling County, ordered Li Jiaomin, the captain of the security team, to lead his troops to pay attention to investigation and arrest at various key intersections. On the 3rd and 4th of this month, 17 cargo cars (including one car) were detained one after another. The cars were full of smuggled goods such as rayon, white sugar, cigarette paper, and drugs. Dozens of Japanese, Koreans, and Chinese escorted the cars. After the detention, the provincial government was reported and asked for instructions on how to deal with it. Chairman Han telegraphed to escort them to Jinan. Li Jiaomin, the head of the security department of the county, escorted them with the police. On the evening of the 4th, they stayed in Shanghe County, and continued south on the 5th. Chairman Han was afraid of accidents, so he sent soldiers from the pistol brigade to meet them at Luokou and escort them to the provincial government. From dawn to noon, the smuggled goods arrived one after another, totaling 74 packages of rayon, 171 packages of white sugar, 23 packages of cloth, 50 packages of cigarette paper, two white boxes, one small leather box, and another 87 packages of drugs (the boxes also contained drugs). After arriving at the provincial government, in addition to checking the vehicles and goods, the Japanese and Koreans were placed in the reception room, and the Chinese were handed over to the military law office for interrogation by Chairman Han. At 2 pm, the Japanese Consul Yano Manabu visited Han at the provincial government, requesting the return of the people and goods. Han replied that he would deal with it after he had inquired. At 3 pm, after inquiring, he handed over eight Japanese and eighteen Koreans to Kan, the director of the Japanese Consulate, and the head of the Japanese Police Department, who were brought back by the provincial government. In addition, officials from the military law office and officials from the Japanese Consulate identified the goods and detained them in the provincial government. The 15 Chinese who drove the cars were escorted to the military law office for appropriate disposal later.

Also, at 1 pm, while the interrogation was in progress, dozens of Japanese, all wearing short clothes, suddenly came to the provincial government and claimed that they wanted to see Chairman Han. Han did not see them because he was busy. The Japanese still refused to leave. The guards of the provincial government then showed their swords and raised their guns, making considerable warning. It was not until the Japanese and Koreans were taken away by the staff of the Japanese Consulate that they began to disperse, without causing any trouble. Also, at 4 pm, Shanghe County also detained a car of smuggled goods and sent it to Luokou. The Japanese in the car lay on the ground to prevent the car from leaving. The goods were still in Luokou that evening and had not arrived at the provincial government.

Three Tragic Changes for the Barge Household

Ji Qingshan, a local resident, is over forty years old and has been working as a barge for a living, traveling between Wuxi and Shanghai, carrying goods for others. A few days ago, Ji loaded hundreds of boxes of kerosene and transported them from Suzhou to Wuxi. However, after traveling only a few miles, the entire ship capsized due to excessive weight, resulting in heavy losses. The next day, the ship was lifted out and transported to Wuxi. When the ship arrived at Dangkou Town in the seventh district of this county, a strong wind suddenly rose, and the mast on the ship broke in response. Qing Shan's son, Rong Gui, was seven years old, and his head was crushed by the mast, and his brain burst, and he died immediately. Until about 11 am the day before yesterday, the ship arrived under the Gongyun Bridge and stopped to unload the kerosene. I don't know how, but the cabin was lost again, and it was out of control. Qing Shan's eldest son, Rong Guan, ten years old, was burned on his left arm, chest, and face. It can be said to be tragic.

Fraudulent Money Arrested and Imprisoned

Qian Hongsheng, a native of Changshou, Jiangyin, in July of this year, under the name of the manager of the Yongxing Coal Mine Company stationed in Xishan, established an office in Zhoushanbang, this county, and contacted all parties, claiming that he would invest 200 yuan to be sent to other counties as manager, 100 yuan as associate, and 50 yuan as a worker. This money would be used as a security deposit for future service. Fu Zuyin, who lives on Tonghui Road, believed it to be true and paid fifty yuan for a worker position. Later, the office moved to the west gate. Fu repeatedly urged Qian, but Qian kept procrastinating. In September, he fled without a trace. Fu knew that he had been deceived and could only call in vain. At 2 pm yesterday, he met Qian Hongsheng at Tonghui Bridge, and often twisted him into the second branch of the public security bureau under his jurisdiction, and transferred him to the general bureau, and then transferred him to the court for interrogation and detention.

Page 9

Local News

Huang Fu Passed Away Yesterday Morning. Mrs. Huang Telegraphed Chairman Lin and Chairman Chiang. All Bureaus and Offices Under the Municipal Government Flew Flags at Half-Mast to Express Grief. The Encoffining Ceremony Will Be Held at the China Funeral Home Tomorrow at 3 PM. His Last Words Offered Loyal Advice to His Countrymen and Neighboring Countries. 85

National Government Member Huang Fu passed away at 9:25 AM yesterday morning at his residence on Qiqi Road in the French Concession, at the age of 57. His close friends during his lifetime, such as Vice President of the Executive Yuan Kong Xiangxi, Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, Industry Minister Wu Dingchang, and former Interior Minister Xu Xiuzhi, all went to offer condolences. His remains are scheduled to be moved to the China Funeral Home on Haig Road at 9 AM this morning, and the encoffining ceremony will be held at 3 PM the day after tomorrow (the 8th). The details are as follows:

Failure to Recover

Huang's liver cancer had shown some improvement after treatment by traditional Chinese medicine practitioners Fan Shisheng and Liu Zhengzi for two months. Unexpectedly, his condition changed suddenly one evening, exacerbated by emotional distress, and the illness worsened. By the morning of the second day, he had fallen into a coma. Although he showed some improvement after medical intervention, his long-term illness made recovery impossible, and he passed away at his residence on Qiqi Road in the French Concession at 9:25 AM yesterday morning. Huang had always been known for his robust health. Two years ago, he began to feel some local discomfort, which gradually worsened. He consulted famous Western doctors from various countries, but after exploratory surgery, it was determined that he had terminal liver cancer, for which there was no effective treatment, and they all gave up. He then consulted traditional Chinese medicine practitioners Fan and Liu, but ultimately, his weakened body could not be saved.

Illness Progression

According to those close to Huang, the progression of his illness was as follows: Huang had always been extremely healthy during his prime. Two years ago, he began to feel some local discomfort, but he initially did not pay much attention to it. After taking charge of the affairs of the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Reorganization Committee, he began to feel overwhelmed by the heavy workload, and various ailments such as nosebleeds and arm pain arose. He sought medical treatment, and his condition improved and relapsed intermittently. This summer, his condition worsened, and Huang was residing in Mogan Mountain. To facilitate medical treatment, he arrived in Shanghai on August 24th and was admitted to Hong En Hospital for treatment on the 27th. After more than a month in the hospital, there was no improvement. To diagnose the root cause of his illness, he underwent surgery at the hospital on September 14th, which revealed that he had liver cancer, deemed a terminal illness, and he refused further treatment. After the surgery, not only was the cancer not removed, but his condition worsened, with abdominal pain and coughing, and a significant decrease in appetite. To alleviate the patient's suffering, the doctors administered heavy doses of anesthetics daily, concluding that Huang's condition would deteriorate rapidly and he would not live much longer. On September 28th, he planned to hire a German expert to fly to Shanghai for treatment, but this did not happen. Later, as famous Western doctors from various countries in Shanghai all gave up, he hired traditional Chinese medicine practitioner Fan Shisheng, who flew from Lushan to Shanghai for treatment. By the time Fan arrived in Shanghai, Huang was already feeling overwhelmed, irritable, and concerned about national affairs. After Fan's careful treatment, there seemed to be hope for recovery. Later, he hired the famous doctor Liu Zhengzi, who came to Shanghai from Shaanxi to assist in the treatment, and his condition improved further. On November 25th, to facilitate taking Chinese medicine, he left the hospital and returned to his residence. On the night of December 1st, his condition suddenly changed. Huang's eldest daughter had already arrived in Shanghai from Beijing to care for him. That night, Huang suddenly felt a stabbing pain, and his condition worsened, leading to a coma. He passed away at 9:25 AM on the morning of the sixth.

Condolences from Friends

Huang was briefly conscious on the afternoon of the fifth, but then lapsed back into unconsciousness. He regained consciousness again at 10 PM, and was able to speak, asking those present about national affairs, and saying that China could only survive if the whole country united to resist invasion. At 2 AM yesterday morning, his condition became more critical. After emergency injections by doctors, he was able to hang on for a few more hours. At around 8 AM, his breathing became intermittent, and his family knew that he could not be saved. They separately notified Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, former Interior Minister Xu Xiuzhi, former Beiping Mayor Yuan Liang, and Municipal Works Bureau Director Shen Yi, among others, by phone to bid him farewell. After Huang's death, Mrs. Huang, Shen Jingying, telegraphed Chairman Lin, Chairman Chiang, and friends in various places to report the news. Vice President of the Executive Yuan Kong Xiangxi, Industry Minister Wu Dingchang, Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission member Xie Zhongfu, and Railway Bureau Director Huang Boqiao, who are currently in Shanghai, all went to offer condolences within an hour of Huang's death. Mayor of Shanghai Wu Tiecheng, Shanghai Garrison Commander Yang Hu, Director of the Foreign Ministry's Shanghai Office Zhou Jue, and Huang's friends during his lifetime all went to offer condolences and pay their respects to his remains in the afternoon.

Establishment of Funeral Committee

Mrs. Huang had been caring for the patient for months, and her health was already failing. Witnessing his death, she was overwhelmed with grief, almost collapsing. Therefore, Huang's funeral arrangements will be handled by his friends Zhang Qun, Xu Xiuzhi, Xu Qingfu (who arrived in Shanghai from Hangzhou yesterday afternoon), Tao Lüqian (who arrived in Shanghai this morning), Yuan Liang, and Shen Yi, among others. A funeral committee will be established immediately, and the funeral committee has issued a separate announcement regarding Huang's funeral arrangements, emphasizing simplicity, as Huang had always disliked superficiality, valued practicality, and possessed the spirit of promoting the New Life Movement. He was also a devout Buddhist, practicing Mahayana Buddhism, and repeatedly spoke of simplicity during his illness. The decision of his friends not to accept any gifts is in line with his wishes and serves to correct social customs. The Encoffining Ceremony Tomorrow.

Huang's remains are scheduled to be moved from his private residence on Qiqi Road to the China Funeral Home on Haig Road at 9 AM this morning. The arrangement of the mourning hall was completed yesterday afternoon. Reception staff will be provided by Huang's friends, and the municipal government will also send staff to assist with the funeral arrangements. Huang's relatives and friends who live in various places will arrive by noon tomorrow. The date of the encoffining ceremony has been set for 3 PM tomorrow (the 8th). More than thirty telegrams of condolence from various places arrived in Shanghai last night.

Flags at Half-Mast to Express Grief

After learning of Huang's death, Mayor Wu immediately telegraphed Nanjing and Luoyang to report to the National Government and President Chiang. As Huang was the first mayor of Shanghai, Mayor Wu ordered all bureaus and offices under the municipal government to fly flags at half-mast for one day to express grief in memory of Huang.

Publication of Last Words

I have lived for fifty-seven years. Recalling my youth, I encountered the difficulties of the Jiawu and Gengzi years. Stirred by patriotic righteousness, I put down my pen and took up arms, discussing ways to save the country with like-minded patriots. The first step was fundamental reform. After going to Japan, I followed Mr. Sun Yat-sen, Ke Qiang, and Yingshi to engage in revolution. With the Xinhai Revolution, I thought we could devote ourselves to construction and disarm and disband soldiers. Unexpectedly, after only one year, this nascent force was crushed. Since then, the struggle between positive and negative forces has undergone several changes until the rise of the National Army in the thirteenth year of the Republic, when the revolutionary forces were deeply rooted in the north. In the fifteenth year of the Republic, the National Revolutionary Army rose up and the revolutionary forces unified the country. In my humble capacity, I participated in these battles, surviving many near-death experiences. I had long resolved to dedicate myself to the country. In recent years, national strength has been insufficient, and foreign aggression has been imminent. Remembering the difficulties of creation by the martyrs and the severity of the current crisis, I ventured to overcome difficulties and accepted the mandate of the Beiping Reorganization Committee to support the north and ease the overall situation. Now, fortunately, construction is advancing rapidly, unification has been completed, and international responses are more than adequate compared to the past. I can die without regret at this time with a melancholic liver disease. However, there is something I cannot forget. An individual life is no more than a grain of millet in a granary, but the life of a nation should coexist with the earth. We are members of the nation, and the life of the nation is our individual life. Taking advantage of my last breath, I offer my last loyal advice to my countrymen and neighboring countries with tears: 1. In times of national crisis, there must be a spirit and action of national unity. Now, our political leader, General Chiang, is loyal to the country, has endured hardships, and has the unshirkable responsibility of leading the revival. The people should transcend subjective emotions and trust him with one heart, doing everything with great sympathy, doing their best to assist, and remembering that the world situation is dangerous and the national destiny is new. In all aspects, inspire the enthusiasm for building the country, do calm work, and accumulate the strength that a modern country should have at the level of the modern era to await the opportunity for national mobilization. The government should also be extremely tolerant of the people, giving full play to its broad-mindedness in selecting and appointing talents, so that the experienced and the promising can express their intelligence and talents, so that there will be no talents left in the wild, and demonstrate the reality of national unity. 2. Eastern civilization has its own great value. There is no reason for the two countries of China and Japan, which share the same race and culture, to harm each other. However, while touting friendship, they are defending their mistakes. After the four northeastern provinces, they are hoping to further plot North China to shield their man-made pseudo-organization. This is not only an impassable road for the 400 million Chinese who have awakened, but will also cause endless disputes. This is not only a great misfortune for us, but also an unsafe path for the neighboring country itself. If this is not changed, the so-called coexistence and co-prosperity will inevitably fall into common decline and chaos. The neighboring country has always respected Confucianism and should urgently consider the meaning of Confucius and Mencius's forgiveness and implement it by resolutely abandoning its attempts in North China, and then seeking a solution to return our sovereignty in the four northeastern provinces, then friendship will naturally be realized and everything will be solved easily. Following this to seek the liberation of the Asian nations, to glorify Eastern civilization, and to create a blessing for mankind, is it not merely the coexistence and co-prosperity of the two countries? The above two points are related to the national and even the ethnic life of Asia. Now that I am about to part ways with the world, the feeling of worrying about the country cannot be suppressed. I respectfully leave these words. November 26, 25th year of the Republic of China.

Huang Fu's Biography

Huang Fu, styled Yingbai, was originally from Songjiang, Jiangsu. Because his father, Mr. Wenzhi, served as an official in eastern Zhejiang, he was born in Baiguan Town, and entered the school in Qiantang, and thus registered his household there. In his youth, he studied and liked mathematics. He first taught at the Anji County School. Later, after witnessing the national disasters of the Jiawu and Gengzi years, he lamented the weakness of the country and entered the Hangzhou Military Academy to study the army. He achieved top grades in the entire school. At that time, many patriots gathered in the school, and there was a secret organization that advocated revolution. Two years later, the entire school selected the best students to study in Japan, and he went to Japan. At that time, the Premier was launching the organization of the Tongmenghui, and Tokyo was the center of the revolutionary movement. He gathered many army students to join the alliance, and in order to realize that revolution must have strength, he formed the "Manhood Corps" among the army comrades of the Tongmenghui, which was later expanded into the "Chengcheng Corps," which was dedicated to implementing plans. He also published the Wuxue magazine. During the restoration of the Xinhai Revolution, the new armies of the provinces responded unexpectedly, which was based on the organization of military comrades. Mr. Huang relied on his superior mathematics and entered the Army Survey Bureau. After graduating, he planned to join the military and became a member of the Military Advisory Office, secretly connecting with comrades in the north. At the beginning of the Xinhai Revolution, he took the opportunity to go south to assist Chen Gong Yingshi in planning the advance, and served as the Chief of Staff of the Shanghai Military Government. He also trained a division himself and served as the commander of the 23rd Division. All the regulations of the Shanghai Army, as well as the joint attack on Nanjing by the armies and the establishment of the provisional government, were largely due to his planning. Later, the General Headquarters of the Nanjing Garrison was established, and Mr. Huang also served as the Director-General of the Garrison. After the unification of the North and South, public opinion focused on reducing the army, and the two governorates of Jiangsu and Shanghai merged, so he served as the Chief of Staff of the Jiangsu Governorate, and he took the lead in disbanding the 23rd Division himself. The following year, the Song case occurred, and the Second Revolution broke out. He assisted Chen Gong Yingshi again in establishing the military department in Shanghai and capturing the manufacturing bureau. He then fled to Japan, and Yuan Shikai offered a large sum of money to capture him. Soon, he went to the United States to study. In the fourth year of the Republic, the Chu'an Society was established, and he returned to Shanghai by a fast route to sponsor the independence of Zhejiang, responding to the provinces of Yunnan and Guangxi. After the matter was settled, he retired to Tianjin to devote himself to writing and lecturing. Except for a period of time when he joined forces with Mr. Zhang Jingyu to advocate the peace movement to support the Dharma-Protecting Army, he did not ask about politics. His famous two works, "The Lessons of the European War and the Future of China" and "The World After the War," were published at this time. In the eighth year of the Republic, he went to the United States again to investigate the economy. Soon after, the Washington Conference was held, and he was ordered to participate. He made many plans for the recovery of Qingdao. After returning to China, Mr. Wang Liangchou formed a cabinet and appointed him to oversee the National Financial Conference. Soon after, Mr. Zhang Jingyu formed a cabinet and took charge of foreign affairs. Later, he entered the cabinet twice to lead education. With his spare strength, he lectured at Peking University and in the army of Mr. Feng Huanzhang in Nanyuan. He was especially close to Feng, and secretly discussed the connection of the national revolutionary front. In the 13th year of the Republic, Feng's National Army returned from Gubeikou and formed the regency cabinet. The Premier went to Tianjin and immediately sent Mr. Wang Jingwei to visit Mr. Huang to discuss everything. As a result, the National Army became a powerful element in expanding the revolutionary base in the north. At that time, General Chiang was working in Guangdong and sent a secret telegram to Mr. Huang, saying that he wished him to serve Mr. Sun as he served his eldest brother, referring to Chen Yingshi. In the 15th year of the Republic, the National Revolutionary Army went to the Yangtze River, and General Chiang welcomed him to Jiangxi, making many suggestions for the progress of the revolution. The National Government established its capital in Nanjing, and he served as the first mayor of Shanghai. In the 17th year of the Republic, he served as the Minister of Foreign Affairs. Later, he went to Mogan Mountain to cultivate himself, study Buddhist scriptures, and established Mogan Elementary School as the center for improving the Mogan Mountain farming village. Before and after the September 18th Incident, he secretly presented many plans to the government authorities to save the situation, and united with celebrities from all walks of life to launch the New China Construction Society to study various construction programs. In the 22nd year, the National Government established the Administrative Yuan in Beiping in a crisis in Tianjin, and specially appointed Mr. Huang as the chairman of the Beiping Political Reorganization Committee, ordering him to rush to Beiping to govern. After two years of negotiations, he became depressed and fell ill. In the 24th year, he asked for leave to return south to recuperate. At first, he thought it was a stomach disease. It was not until the spring of this year that he learned it was a liver disease. In the early autumn, he entered Hongen Hospital, where doctors tried to cure it with surgery, but only then did he learn that it was liver cancer. Later, he took Chinese medicine, which he felt was effective, but ultimately the root of the disease was too deep, and he passed away at the hour of the day on December 6. He has two daughters, the eldest named Xiwen and the second named Xizhi. Before his death, he was still concerned about national affairs and left a will, which was recorded by his wife, Shen Jingying, and he instructed his wife to be frugal with the funeral and use the remaining money to run education.

Fisheries Syndicate Held Preparatory Meeting Yesterday 91

Decided to use fishermen as the object of the syndicate's lending, improve the organization of fishermen, improve production and marketing, and allocate 10,000 yuan for preparatory expenses, scheduled to be established next spring.

The Fisheries Syndicate, jointly formed by the Ministry of Industry and China Communications and other twelve banks, held its third preparatory meeting at the Hong Kong Road Bank Club at 3 pm yesterday. Yu Zhenyong, Director of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department of the Ministry of Industry, Cheng Muhao of China Communications, Cao Jiru, Cai Jinsheng of Siming, Ye Fuxiao of the Mainland, Chen Jianhan of the South, Wang Shaoxian of the Salt Industry, Yang Peichang of Jin Cheng, Dong Chengdao of Shanghai, Sun Renjing of Zhejiang Industrial, Wang Zhixin of Xinhua (representing Sun Ruihuang), Yao Yinpeng of Zhonghui, Gui Yanfang, Qian Xinzhi of the Four Banks Savings Society, Zhou Desun, etc. attended. Design committee members Qu Junyuan and Hua Wenyu attended the meeting. Yu Zhenyong presided over the meeting. First, the chairman reported on the Ministry's hopes for the Fisheries Syndicate, and then the chairman of the preparatory office, Qian Xinzhi, reported on the recent preparations. Then, the meeting discussed the lending methods and the improvement of production and marketing. The meeting adjourned at 4:45.

Lending Method

After the meeting, according to the design committee member Hua Wenyu's words to the Xin Xin News Agency reporter, the three resolutions of the meeting, in addition to the report on the recent preparations by Qian Xinzhi, the chairman of the preparatory office, the representatives exchanged opinions on the lending method. The results of the discussion were: The lending object was decided to be fishermen, because fishermen are direct producers; (2) Improve the organization of fishermen, because Chinese fishermen do not yet have a sound organization, so after investigating the current organization and economic situation of fishermen, provide assistance; (3) Hope that the Ministry of Industry will pay attention to production and marketing and improve them to seek development, so that future lending will be guaranteed.

Establishment Next Spring

The official establishment date of the Fisheries Syndicate has been scheduled for the spring fish season next year. Of all the funds of one million yuan, the fixed capital of 200,000 yuan from the Ministry of Industry has been fixed in the budget by the Ministry of Industry and can be allocated at any time. Now, 10,000 yuan has been allocated first for preparatory expenses. The floating capital of 800,000 yuan from the participating banks has been prepared. Once the syndicate is established, it can be allocated. The preparatory office of the syndicate is actively conducting investigation work. In addition to preparing forms and sending them to various fishery agencies or groups to assist in collecting materials, it has also sent investigators Cao Erwei and others to the Shengsi Islands production area to conduct on-the-spot investigations of the economic, production, and various related actual conditions of fishermen to serve as a reference for future lending and the development of fisheries.

This is to the Aviation Construction Association, Shanghai Branch.

The Actual Situation of Improvement in the Past Year

Beining Railway Affairs

China Merchants Bureau Arranges for Unemployed Workers 99
